-some variables are sked and doesn't seems to have normal dist
(#ndvi_mean_var_182_365-there is no temporal steadiness of the
vegetation activity between the different parcels -rpearson have two
main peaks in the beginning of the season and in the end of the
season-peak imply a good catch crop cultivation -ndvi_trend have a high
curtosis and it seeem most of the parcels have a main day in which there
is a successful catch crop cultivation (harvesting,plowing,frost) -some
variables have unique values and should be considered to be converted
into dummies variables for the ease of statistical analysis:
#number_level_shifts_182_365-variable imply the day of abrupt change in
the parcel, #monthly and time series temperature features/#monthly
relative humidity features/#monthly precipitation features,#monthly soil
temp features, #monthly sunsine duration features,- those values taken
for all the parcels in the main geographic area.

some of the data is skewed, let's check the asymetry of the
probabilility distribution

    def powerlight (df):
        vn= df_cc_numeric.columns
        d = {}
        for v in vn :
            sk= df_cc_numeric[v].skew()
            if (sk>1) | (sk<-1) :
                pn= '+'
            else:
                pn= "-"
            d[v]= {'variable' : v, 'skew' : sk, 'result': pn}
        return pd.DataFrame(d).transpose() 
         

     powerlight(df_cc_numeric)

#good correlation between ndvi_min_182_365 and sunshine duration , temp
(soil, environment, min_max ratio), relative humidity,

    var_correlation = pd.DataFrame(columns=['var1','var2','spearman_corr','p-val'])
    for i in df_cc_numeric.columns:
            for j in df_cc_numeric.columns:
                b= "{}/{}".format(i,j)
                c= "{}/{}".format(j,i)
                if i != j:
                    if (c not in var_correlation.index):
                        mask= ~np.isnan(df_cc_numeric[i]) & ~np.isnan(df_cc_numeric[j])
                        a= stats.spearmanr(df_cc_numeric[i][mask], df_cc_numeric[j][mask])
                        var_correlation.loc[b] = [i,j,abs(a[0]),a[1]]

    var_correlation_filtered= var_correlation.loc[(var_correlation['spearman_corr']> 0.7) & (var_correlation['p-val']< 0.05)]
    var_correlation_filtered.sort_values(by= ['spearman_corr'], ascending= False)

Data Cleansing

Outliers detection

    plt.figure(figsize=(22,222))

    def outliers_detection (df):
        for i, col in enumerate(df.columns):
            if col != 'class':
                ax= plt.subplot(55,3,i+1)
                sns.boxplot(data= df, x= col, ax=ax)
                plt.subplots_adjust(hspace= 0.8)
                plt.title('boxplot:{}'.format(col), fontsize=20)
                plt.xlabel('{}'.format(col),fontsize=14)
                
    outliers_detection(df_cc_numeric)

[]

    #correlation analysis with or without outliers
    #if correlation and distribution change within outliers removal, we can't remove the outliers in the feature
    #in any other state we can remove the outliers

    numeric_var= df_cc_numeric.select_dtypes(include=[np.number])

    def Outlier_Matrix(df):
        for i in df.columns:
            q1= df[i].quantile(0.25)
            q3= df[i].quantile(0.75)
            iqr=q3-q1
            lower= q1-1.5*iqr
            upper= q3+1.5*iqr
            x=np.array(df[i])
            x=x.astype("float")
            b=[]
            for j in x:
                if j>upper or j<lower :
                    b.append(1)
                else:
                    b.append(0)
            df[i]=b
        return df

    #numeric_var= pd.Series([df_cc_numeric,np.nan])
    df_cc_numeric_out= Outlier_Matrix(numeric_var)
    df_cc_numeric_out

    #LET'S USE THE COCOR FUNCTION TO CHECK WHETHER THE OUTLIERS REMOVAL AFFECTS CORRELATION AND DISTRIBUTION 
    from scipy.stats import norm
    def cocor (x1,x2,y1,y2):
        xy1= x1.corr(y1, method= "spearman")
        xy2= x2.corr(y2, method= "spearman")
        n1= len(x1)
        n2= len(x2)
        xy_z= 0.5* np.log((1+xy1)/(1-xy1))
        ab_z= 0.5* np.log((1+xy2)/(1-xy2))
        if n2 is None:
            n2=n1
        se_diff_r= np.sqrt(1/(n1-3)+1/(n2-3))
        diff= xy_z - ab_z
        z= abs(diff - se_diff_r)
        p= (1-norm.cdf(z)) *2
        return z,p

    #let's check if the change is significance and if we can delete the outliers
    corr_distribution_check= pd.DataFrame(columns=['var','ol_cnt','ol_pct','dist_changed','corr_changed'])
    col=df_cc_numeric_out.columns
    np.seterr(divide='ignore',invalid= 'ignore')
    for i in col:
    #col with outliers
        ol=df_cc[i]
    #col without outliers
        non= df_cc_numeric[i].loc[df_cc_numeric_out[i]==0]
    #target varible with outliers
        class_ol=df_cc['class']
    #target variable without outliers
        class_non=df_cc['class'].loc[df_cc_numeric_out[i]==0]
        
        p, p_value=cocor(ol,class_ol,non,class_non)
        corr_changed= np.where(p_value<0.05,'+','-')

        ol=df_cc_numeric_out.sum()
        ol_pct= df_cc_numeric_out[i].sum()*100/len(df_cc_numeric)
        pval=stats.ks_2samp(ol,non)[1]
        dis_changed=np.where(pval<0.05,'+','-')
        cor_dist_check= corr_distribution_check.append({'var':i, 'ol_cnt':ol, 'ol_pct':ol_pct, 'dist_changed':dis_changed,'corr_changed':corr_changed},ignore_index=True)
    cor_dist_check

    #create indicators 1,0 for the MV
    def missing_dect(df):
        col= df.columns
        mv_df= pd.DataFrame(columns= col)
        for i in col:
            for j in range(len(df)):
                if pd.isna(df.loc[j,i])==True:
                    mv_df.loc[j,i]= 1
                else:
                    mv_df.loc[j,i]= 0
        return mv_df

    missing_dect(df_cc_numeric)

    #let's check the missing values mechanism (kolmogorov-smirnov test)
    #if missingness is random (distribution doesn't change), no feature can explain the missigness, imputation can be done using KNN or Mice
    #if missingness is not random (distribution changed), we can't do imputation, we might change to categorical variables
    mv_dist_check= pd.DataFrame(columns=['var','mv_cnt','mv_prc','distribution_changed'])
    mv_no_cat_var= df_cc.drop(['class','area'],1)
    mv_col=mv_no_cat_var.columns
    np.seterr(divide='ignore',invalid='ignore')
    for i in mv_col:
    #columns with missing values    
        mv_with=df_cc[i]
    #columns without missing values
        mv_without=df_cc[i].loc[mv_cc[i]==0]
    #target varibale with missing values
        class_mv=df_cc['class']
    #target variable without missing values
        class_mv_without=df_cc['class'].loc[mv_cc[i]==0]
        mv_sum=mv_cc[i].sum()
        mv_prc=mv_cc[i].sum()/len(df_cc[i])*100
    #ks test
        p_value=stats.ks_2samp(mv_with,mv_without)[1]
        dist_changed=np.where(p_value<0.05,'+','-')
        mv_dist_check=mv_dist_check.append({'var':i, 'mv_cnt':mv_sum,'mv_prc': mv_prc,'distribution_changed':dist_changed},ignore_index=True)
    mv_dist_check

#in varibles with random 'yes'(p-value>0.05), imputation could be
executed (% missing is low)>>>no other variable can explain the
missingess

#in variables with random 'no', no imputation could be executed.

    #let's make a new data frame for the missing varibles with the random 'no' and compare their dist with or without missing
    new_var_rand_no=list(mv_dist_check['var'].loc[mv_dist_check['distribution_changed']=='+'])
    df_no_mv=df_cc.dropna()
    col_na=df_no_mv.columns
    a=len(new_var_rand_no)
    b=2
    c=1

    fig=plt.figure(figsize=(30,50))
    plt.subplots_adjust(hspace=0.7)

    for i in new_var_rand_no:
        for j in df_no_mv:
            if i==j:
                plt.subplot(a,b,c)
                plt.title('{}'.format(i))
                plt.xlabel(i)
                sns.kdeplot(df_cc[i],fill=True)
                sns.kdeplot(df_no_mv[j],fill=True)
                plt.legend(labels=['with_mv','without_mv'])
                c=c+1
    plt.show()

#using visualization we can see that missing mechnism for the not random

not depends on the user.

    #let see the heat map of the variables with the MNAR mechanism
    plt.subplots_adjust(hspace=1.5)
    for i in new_var_rand_no:
        var_sort=df_cc.sort_values(i)
        plt.title('{}'.format(i))
        msno.matrix(var_sort)

    import os
    #convert the object types variable to categorical object type with codes assign to them
    cat_code=[]
    for i in range(0,df_cc.shape[1]):
        if(df_cc.iloc[:,i].dtype=='object'):
            df_cc.iloc[:,i]=pd.Categorical(df_cc.iloc[:,i])
            df_cc.iloc[:,i]=df_cc.iloc[:,i].cat.codes
            df_cc.iloc[:,i]=df_cc.iloc[:,i].astype('object')
            cat_code.append(df_cc.columns[i])
    cat_code

    ['area']

    #let's see the correlations of the variables before and after
    numeric_df_cc_imputed= df_cc_imputed.select_dtypes(include=np.number)
    numeric_df_cc_imputed_col= numeric_df_cc_imputed.columns
    df_cc_imputed_corr= pd.DataFrame(columns=('var1','var2','original_corr','abs_corr','p-value'))
    for i in numeric_df_cc_imputed_col:

    #perform anova test between the numeric variables and the target variable (class)
    numeric_df_cc_imputed=numeric_df_cc_imputed.join(class_vr)
    from scipy.stats import f_oneway
    aov_class= pd.DataFrame(columns=('var1','var2','p_value'))
    for i in numeric_df_cc_imputed.columns:
        if i!= 'class':
            Cat_list=numeric_df_cc_imputed.groupby('class')[i].apply(list)
            aov = f_oneway(*Cat_list)
            b= '{}'.format(i)
            aov_class.loc[b]=['class',i,aov[1]]

some conclusions:

#there might be some attributes that highly affects the target feature
(e.g. Class): -Av_relative_humidity_july, -Av_relative_humidity_aug,
-Av_relative_humidity_sep, -Av_relative_humidity_oct,
-Av_relative_humidity_nov Those features have relatively high
correlation with the feature NDVI_SUM_232_272, in which define the rate
of chlorophil in the parcel (e.g. the level of green cover of the
crop/cultivar). as the NDVI_SUM_232_272 higher, parcel have more green
cover between 21/08 and 30/09 and it might be due to cover crop 16/02 in
the next year and it probably due to cover crop consolidation (cultivar
may be already harvested).

-Av_soil_temp_jan , Av_soil_temp_sep. as they decrease, NDVI_SUM_001_046
increase. -Av_soil_temp_march, as it increase, NDVI_SUM_001_046 increase
(higher deployment of the cover crop, mean higher soil temp in march,
this must be due to cover crop, as the cultivar is still in winter
dormancy and doesn't have canopy in which will affect the soil temp).
-sunshine_duration_sep, as it decrease, NDVI_SUM_001_046 increase.

This features might get higher weight in defining the best model using the next step of the classification using machine learning.
